WELL EVALUATION
WELL EVALUATION
Oxy USA, Inc.
Delvin Dukart 6-30-31H-143-95
Figure 1. Nabors X-20 at the Oxy USA, Inc. Delvin Dukart 6-30-31H-143-95 well on August 8, 2014; 2 miles South of Manning in
Dunn County, ND. (Photo by M. Williamson, Payzone Geologist)
INTRODUCTION
The Oxy USA, Inc. Delvin Dukart 6-30-31H-143-95 [SESW Sec 19, T143N, R95W] is located
approximately 2 miles South of Manning, North Dakota. The subject well was drilled in Dunn County, ND
by the Nabors X-20 rig in the Manning Field of the Bakken pool. The subject well was planned with one
approximately 10,083' [Intermediate casing to projected total depth (TD)] long southerly lateral bore with
intent to intersect regional hydraulic fracture trends that might enhance reservoir quality within the Middle
Bakken. OXY USA intends to develop oil production in the late Devonian Middle Bakken target porosity
zone with a stratigraphy consisting of siltstone, silty sandstone and limestone with depositional lithofacies
ranging from onshore terrestrial to offshore marine deposits.
ENGINEERING
Surface, Vertical & Curve Operations:
A 9 " surface hole was drilled on July 19 and 20, 2014 by the Nabors X-20 rig and surface
casing was set at 2,118'. The vertical hole operations commenced on August 3, 2014 with Weatherford
providing equipment and personnel for MWD and directional drilling services. The first vertical Bottom
Hole Assembly (BHA), consisting of MWD tools, 1.50° bend Hunting 7/8 5.7 motor and Smith MDSi616
BPX PDC bit (6x16 jets), drilled to the kick off point (KOP) of 9,682' and was then exchanged for the
curve assembly. The first curve BHA consisted of a 1.83º bend NOV Gyro Data 7/8 5.8 motor, 8 ¾"
Security MMD55M bit containing 5x18 jets and new MWD tools. This assembly reached a curve TD of
10,987' MD (10,446' TVD). This placed the well bore approximately 12' into a 26' thick (shale to shale)
Middle Bakken zone, and 4' into the 10' thick silty sandstone targeted interval. This BHA drilled the
7.5°/100', 1,305' long curve in 29.99 hours with no issues.
No E-logs were run due to the close proximity of the Delvin Dukart 5-30-31H-143-95 and Delvin
Dukart 3-30-31H-143-95, both of which drilled all the way through the Bakken Formation. Directional tools
were then pulled out of the hole and a string of 7" intermediate casing was run, set, and cemented at a
depth of 10,970' MD. Lateral operations continued on August 31, 2014. Diesel invert drilling fluid was
used throughout the vertical hole and curve build sections maintaining a 9.8-10.1 ppg mud weight for
stable downhole conditions.
Lateral Operations:
Weatherford again provided equipment and personnel for MWD and directional drilling services.
The directional drillers, MWD hands, and Payzone geologists worked closely together throughout the
project to make steering decisions in order to maximize the amount of borehole exposure to the pay zone.
A five-bladed 6" bit (Smith MDi613), 1.50º Hunting mud motor, and MWD tools comprised the first
lateral BHA (4th BHA overall) and was run in the hole on 4" drill pipe starting at 10,987' MD. This BHA
reached a TD of 20,938' in 108.94 hours, making a one run, 6.5 day lateral. Moreover, spud to TD was a
total of 17 days. The lateral resulted in a TD of 20,938' MD (10,338.20' TVD) at a final azimuth of 176.37º,
resulting in a closure vertical section of 10,822.45'. The BHL is 10,800.72' South & 685.47' East from
surface location or approx. 258.19' FNL & 2,685.47' FWL SW SE Sec. 31, T143N, R95W (Figure 2).
Salt water drilling fluid was used from the intermediate casing to TD with mud weights throughout
the lateral varying from 9.7+-10.2+ ppg.

GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods:
Geologic supervision of the well was provided by Payzone Consulting, Inc. with three well site geologists.
Mike Williamson and Kevin Jacks drilled the vertical and curve, and Brandon Lutz and Mike Williamson
drilled the horizontal sections. A CanrigTM gas chromatograph was interfaced with a Rigwatch electronic
data recorder system and provided total gas information for viewing around location. Lagged samples
were caught in 30' intervals from 8,000'-10,700' with 10' samples collected when landing the curve from
10,700'-10,987' MD. 100' lagged samples were collected through out the lateral (10,990'-20,938' TD)
Cuttings were examined under a binocular microscope and complete lithologic descriptions are provided
in the lithology document within this evaluation. Two sets of dry cuttings were collected, with one set sent
to the North Dakota Geological Survey Core Library and the second set sent to Jennifer Califf, the project
geologist overseeing operations.
Lithology and Geologic Interpretation:
Geologic evaluation began at 8,000' within the Tyler Formation [Pennsylvanian; Minnelusa Group]. The
first top that was used for landing was the Kibbey "Lime" (within the Kibbey Formation) [Mississippian;
Big Snowy Group] which was penetrated at 8,394' TVD (-6,098'). Samples from this interval were
described as:
8390-8420 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray to gray, light gray to brown, microcrystalline, blocky, firm to hard, trace
pellet, no visible porosity; SILTSTONE: light gray, light brown to red, tan, trace off white to cream, blocky, soft to friable,
sandy in part, anhydrite in part, calcareous cement
The top of the 1st Charles Salt [Mississippian, Madison Group] was penetrated at 8,605' TVD (-6,312').
Within the Charles formation, the Green Point Anhydrite (GP Anhydrite) was penetrated at 8,820' TVD
(-6,527') and the Base of the Last Charles Salt (BLS) was drilled at 8,904' TVD (-6,611'). Samples from
this interval were described as:
8870-8900 SALT: milky, clear, crystalline, hard, euhedral to subhedral; ARGILLACEOUS LIMESTONE: mudstone to
packstone, gray, light gray, very fine crystalline, no visible porosity
8900-8930 LIMESTONE: mudstone, tan to light brown, trace gray, cryptocrystalline to microcrystalline, blocky, soft to firm,
chalky to crystalline texture, trace dense, argillaceous in part, dolomitic in part, no visible porosity; occasional
ANHYDRITE: white, cream, amorphous, very soft, earthy texture
The top of the Mission Canyon Formation [Mississippian; Madison Group] was drilled at 9,085' TVD
(-6,792'). The prospective Fryburg interval (within the Mission Canyon Formation) was penetrated at
9,260' TVD (-6,967'). The Mission Canyon consisted of interbedded limestone, dolomites, and
anhydrites. Dolomite in the mid to lower Mission Canyon showed fair-moderate intercrystalline porosity to
traces of pinpoint porosity. The samples for this interval were described as:
9110-9140 LIMESTONE: mudstone to wackestone, light gray, gray, blocky, firm, dense, crystalline to earthy, slightly
argillaceous, no visible porosity; ANHYDRITE: cream, crystalline, soft, amorphous in part
9140-9170 ANHYDRITE: cream, crystalline, soft, amorphous in part; trace LIMESTONE: mudstone to wackestone, light
gray, gray, blocky, firm, dense, crystalline to earthy, slightly argillaceous, no visible porosity
The argillaceous limestone signifying the top of the Lodgepole Formation [Mississippian; Madison
Group] was penetrated at 9,593' TVD (-7,300') with 807' TVD of consistent lithology described as:
9590-9620 ARGILLACEOUS LIMESTONE: mudstone, medium gray, medium gray to brown, trace dark gray, hard,
earthy, dolomitic in part, trace pyrite, no visible porosity
The False Bakken (Carrington Shale) within the Lodgepole Formation was drilled at 10,674' MD;
10,400' TVD (-8,107'). The False Bakken was described as:
10670-10700 SHALE: medium gray to dark gray, firm to hard, blocky, earthy texture, common disseminated pyrite,
carbonaceous, trace calcite, no visible porosity; trace ARGILLACEOUS LIMESTONE: as above
The carbonaceous, petroliferous Upper Bakken Shale signifying the top of the Bakken Formation was
penetrated at 10,748' MD; 10,421' TVD (-8,128') and was described as:
10740-10760 SHALE: dark brown, black, blocky, soft to friable, earthy texture, abundant disseminated pyrite, pyrite
fracture fill, common nodules pyrite, carbonaceous, petroliferous, no visible porosity; trace LIMESTONE: as above
The Middle Bakken was penetrated at 10,808' MD; 10,433' TVD (-8,140'). The stratigraphy of the Middle
Bakken consisted of varying thicknesses of siltstone and silty sandstone. (Figure 3) The packstone bed
that occasionally occurs was not present.
Figure 3. Generalized lithology of the Middle Bakken Member
The Middle Bakken was generally described as:
10800-10820 SILTSTONE: medium gray to gray, common medium gray brown, rare cream, friable, sub blocky,
calcareous cement, moderately cemented, common disseminated pyrite, trace intergranular porosity, trace light brown
spotty oil stain; common SILTY SANDSTONE: off white to cream, very fine to fine grained, loose, sub blocky, sub angular
to sub round, moderately sorted, calcareous cement, poorly cemented, sucrosic texture, trace disseminated pyrite, trace
intergranular porosity (Figure 4)
10840-10870 SILTY SANDSTONE: off white to cream, very fine to fine grained, loose, sub blocky, sub angular to sub
round, moderately sorted, calcareous cement, poorly cemented, sucrosic texture, trace disseminated pyrite, trace
intergranular porosity (Figure 5)
Figure 4 and 5. Wet cutting of the Middle Bakken siltstone (left) and silty sandstone (right)*
11270-11300 SILTY SANDSTONE: off white to cream, light gray to gray, light gray brown, very fine grained, friable, sub
rounded to sub angular, calcareous cement, moderately sorted, rare disseminated pyrite, trace intergranular porosity,
possible fracture porosity, trace spotty to even light brown oil stain (Figure 6)
Figure 6. Wet cuttings of the Middle Bakken silty sandstone (close-up, left) with main matrix of the in 10' target window (right)*
*All photos: 45x (M. Williamson, Payzone Well site Geologist)
OFFSET CONTROL INFORMATION
(1) Oxy USA Inc. Delvin Dukart 4 30-31H-143-95 [SESW Sec. 19, T143N, R95W] drilled approximately
40' East of the subject well.
(2) Oxy USA Inc. Kubik Trust 4-19-18H-143-95 [SESW Sec. 19, T143N, R95W] drilled approximately ¼
mile East of the subject well.
(3) Oxy USA Inc. Delvin Dukart 5-30-31H-143-95 [SESW Sec. 19, T143N, R95W] drilled approximately
40' East of the subject well. (Figure 7)
Figure 7. Key offset wells used to decipher Middle Bakken target landing
Kick off point for the curve was established from the offset wells' distance of the "base last salt" marker to
the Middle Bakken target zone. The "base last salt to target" approximation suggested a landing target of
10,449' TVD. The False Bakken was encountered at a TVD of 10,400': 2' below its prognosis depth.
Payzone geologists collaborated with the OXY USA prospect geologist and decided to maintain the
previous landing target of 10,449' TVD. The wellbore was landed 14' below the UBS (approximately
10,446' TVD) and 4' into the 10' thick target zone.
LATERAL GEOLOGY
Gamma Signature:
Within the Middle Bakken silty sandstone and siltstone target interval, gamma counts varied between 29
and 106 API. The packstone was not present throughout the lateral. The top of the target zone was
characterized by a ratty gamma signature ranging from mid 50's up to 106 API. A cleaner, cooler hard
streak was present at and around the center of the target interval and registered low 30's to low 40's API.
The gamma signature below the hard streak was tighter, ranging between mid-high 40's and 60 API. This
"high and tight" signature was a clear indicator of when the wellbore dropped into the lower portion of the
target zone.

Figure 8. Middle Bakken target zone lithology, gamma signature, and interpretive TVD Log.
The entire well bore was drilled in between the ~26' projected shale to shale zone with excellent gamma
markers and trends that represented the stratigraphy within the lateral. These markers and trends aided
geo-steering tremendously. The wellbore was in Middle Bakken throughout the entire lateral and 88%
within the 10' targeted interval.
These gamma markers were used for determining formation dip and depth within the target interval and
permitted efficient geosteering. They are plotted on the Wellsite horizontal log (Figure 9) and dip profile
(Figure 10).

Silty Sandstone (2-5' below center of target zone and below the hard streak; 40's-50'sAPI)
Figure 9. Gamma values (0-100 API scale) depicting stratigraphic marker intervals throughout the target zone.
Geo-steering:
The target zone within the Middle Bakken was established based on the best drill rates, gamma markers
and gas concentrations. A 10' zone of >6% porosity was expected to be encountered in the targeted
interval. Samples from the target zone varied in porosity, oil staining, color, cementation, and pyrite
content. Stratigraphic locations in the target zone were based on drill rates, gas shows, gamma ray
values and sample observations.
The Middle Bakken was penetrated at 10,808' MD; 10,433' TVD and consisted of siltstone and silty
sandstone when landing the curve. The wellbore stayed within the 10' targeted interval for approximately
8,898' of 10,070' or 88% (entry of 10' target to TD). The well was drilled in between the 26' shale to shale
target zone for 100% of the lateral. Using the provided offset log information and the structural data
provided from Oxy USA Inc., Payzone geologists were able to anticipate and interpret the dip rate for the
well. The TVD of the formation decreased 44.80' over 10,070' (Middle Bakken entry to TD projection at
bit) resulting in an overall up dip of 0.28º or 90.28°.
A total depth of 20,938' was reached on September 6, 2014 at 23:00 MST. Total depth resulted in 100%
overall exposure within the Middle Bakken Member of the Bakken Formation and 88% within the defined
10' targeted interval. (Figure 10)

Hydrocarbons:
During the drilling of the lateral, gas readings were recorded, imported/exported, and analyzed via a
CanrigTM gas detection system. The line was hooked up to the gas sniffer and hard-lined into the base of
the possum belly. This permitted consistent and accurate readings of the gas released from the reservoir.
Background gas increased throughout the length of the well, with readings as low as 650 units at the
beginning of the lateral, and as high as the CanrigTM 5436 unit maximum near the end. Connection gases
reached as high as 5436 units with an average of ~4000 units at connections.
Gas values were highest in the zone 2-3' above the center of the targeted interval (Figure 11). Flares
were low (on average 2-4' high) despite the gas detector being maxed out at 5436 units. There was no
significant trip gas observed for the Delvin Dukart 6-30-31H-143-95. Oil show in samples consisted of
even to spotty golden brown oil stain.

Summary

The X-20 drilling rig successfully drilled a two-section horizontal wellbore within the Middle
Bakken Member of the Bakken Formation at the OXY USA, Inc. Delvin Dukart 6-30-31H-143-95.

A mud program consisting of diesel invert (9.7-10.2 ppg) was used from spud to curve landing
with salt water drilling fluid used from the intermediate casing to 20,938' MD (TD). Salt water mud
(9.8-10.1 ppg) was efficient for maintaining stable down hole conditions and permitted adequate
analysis of gas concentrations in the lateral. Background gas concentrations ranged from 650-
5436+ units with connections as high as 5436 units.

Steering was accomplished by sample evaluation and by following correlative drilling rate and
MWD gamma ray markers; making dip estimations based on intersections of these markers with
the well bore. Projections of dip were successfully used to maintain the well bore within the
Middle Bakken. A net of 8,898' (88%) of gross 10,070' of the lateral was drilled in the ideal 10'
thick Middle Bakken target with 100% exposure within the 26' shale to shale Middle Bakken
Member of the Bakken Formation.

Samples from the target consisted of white to off-white, light brown, trace light gray, and light gray
to light brown to brown, tan, trace gray brown and off white. Traces of intergranular porosity were
seen throughout the lateral. Samples from the ideal zone contained a spotty to even brown oil
stain.

A hard streak was present in the center of the target zone, which would occasionally deflect the
well bore when approaching from beneath. This allowed for the well bore to track for short
segments of the lateral, but the assembly's tendency to build overpowered the hard streak's
deflecting ability.

The Delvin Dukart 6-30-31H-143-95 was a successful drilling effort as measured by gross
exposure to the target. The well will be fitted with a 4 ½" production liner and swell packers in
preparation for a fracture stimulation that will determine the true commercial value of the well.
Respectfully submitted,
Brandon Lutz
Mike Williamson
Payzone Consulting, Inc.

LITHOLOGY
Delvin Dukart 6-30-31H-143-95 Lithology
Rig crews caught samples in 30' intervals from 8,000' to 10,700', 10' intervals from
10,700' to 10,990', and 100' intervals from 10,990' to 20,938' (TD). Formation tops and
lithologic markers have been inserted into the sample descriptions below for reference.
Sample descriptions began in the Tyler Formation. Samples were examined wet and dry
under a binocular microscope and were checked for hydrocarbon cut fluorescence
during the lateral. Sample cuts are masked by invert mud through 10,970' (intermediate
casing) where the invert mud was exchanged to a saltwater mud from 10,970' to 20,938'.
Quantifiers in order of increasing abundance are trace, rare, occasional, common and
abundant. Subsea is delineated as the negative numbers within the parentheses located
next to the measured depth or true vertical depth. Sample quality was good to excellent,
but contaminated with lube in some samples. Overall, the samples within the Middle
Bakken target consisted of silty sandstone with grains that varied from off-white, white,
light to medium brown with traces of tan to light cream, and light grey in color. Siltstone
was present above the top of the target window. Variances occurred throughout the
lateral and are noted below.
Drilling in Tyler Formation (Pennsylvanian; Minnelusa Group)________________________________
8000-8030 SHALE: medium to dark gray, black, soft, blocky, earthy texture, occasional disseminated pyrite, silty to sandy in part;
rare DOLOMITE LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, microcrystalline, blocky, firm, earthy texture, calcareous in part, no
visible porosity

rare DOLOMITE LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, microcrystalline, blocky, firm, earthy texture, calcareous in part, no
visible porosity

rare DOLOMITE LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, microcrystalline, blocky, firm, earthy texture, calcareous in part, no
visible porosity

Dear Leslie:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 20727, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than
the 200' setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the
1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 30 & 31 T143N R95W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: The offsite cuttings pit shown on the plats must be approved by the NDIC
field inspector prior to use. In cases where a spacing unit is accessed from an off-site drill pad, an
affidavit must be provided affirming that the surface owner of the multi-well pad agrees to accept burial
on their property of the cuttings generated from drilling the well(s) into an offsite spacing/drilling unit.
Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be
maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out,
completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are conducted. OXY USA Inc. must take into
consideration NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety Regulation) when contemplating simultaneous operations on
the above captioned location. Pursuant to NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety Regulation) "No boiler, portable
electric lighting generator, or treater shall be placed nearer than 150 feet to any producing well or oil
tank." OXY USA INC must contact NDIC Field Inspector Nicole Nelson at 701-290-1527 prior to
location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing
point is: 710' south. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the
well head is: 10862' south.
Leslie Teufel Reeves
June 26, 2014
Page 2
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested
that notification be given immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the
Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal
location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are
8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a
message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys
must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may
require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov
Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

I, William H. Dolinar, Professional Land Surveyor, ND. RLS #6550, hereby certify that (in accordance with a request from Mike Anderson with Oxy USA, Inc., 3239 Highway
22, Dickinson, North Dakota 58601) I and/or personnel under my direction made a survey on the 22nd day of May 2014, for the Surface Hole Location and Placement and
Elevation of platted well, being located within the SE1/4 SW1/4 of Section 19, T143N, R95W of the 5th P.M., Dunn County, State of North Dakota.
Notes: All Azimuths are based on the South line of the Southwest Quarter of Section 19, T143N, R95W of the 5th P.M., being an Azimuth of 269°35'17" using GPS observations,
occupying a WHS control point (5/8" rebar) and having the Location and Elevation derived from an OPUS Solution. Azimuths shown have been rotated 1°39'16.15842" West
from SPC Grid bearings to Geodetic North, based on convergence angle provided by a conversion using Corpscon.
Vertical Datum used is of NAVD 88.
Control Point is located 300°48'21" a distance of 14,291.95 feet from the South Quarter Corner of Section 19, T143N, R95W of the 5th P.M.
Distances shown are Ground Distances using a combined scale factor of 1.000150481.
Location shown here on is not an "ASBUILT" location.
